	<script type="application/ld+json" class="yoast-schema-graph">{"@context":"https://schema.org","@graph":[{"@type":"Article","@id":"https://www.cynet.com/blog/orion-threat-alert-flight-of-the-bumblebee/#article","isPartOf":{"@id":"https://www.cynet.com/blog/orion-threat-alert-flight-of-the-bumblebee/"},"author":{"name":"George Tubin","@id":"https://www.cynet.com/#/schema/person/9b306ab04ef5e25f9fb89c998a6aedab"},"headline":"Orion Threat Alert: Flight of the BumbleBee","datePublished":"2022-04-14T21:27:58+00:00","dateModified":"2025-08-06T14:32:16+00:00","mainEntityOfPage":{"@id":"https://www.cynet.com/blog/orion-threat-alert-flight-of-the-bumblebee/"},"wordCount":1940,"commentCount":0,"publisher":{"@id":"https://www.cynet.com/#organization"},"image":["https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/12/blog-bg-threat-3.jpg"],"thumbnailUrl":"https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/12/blog-bg-threat-3.jpg","keywords":["Cyber Attack|Incident Response|Threat Assessment","Orion","research"],"articleSection":["Threat Alerts"],"inLanguage":"en-US","url":"https://www.cynet.com/blog/orion-threat-alert-flight-of-the-bumblebee/","articleBody":"Cynet’s Threat Research and Intelligence team recently discovered a new malware campaign called BumbleBee. The campaign is unique in its use of Initial Access Brokers’ (IAB) tactics to gain access to victims’ machines. In this post, we will cover what this campaign is, and how the IAB distributes the BumbleBee malware and its TTPs. We will also explain each TTP according to the MITRE ATT&amp;CK model, and its purpose. A new campaign in the wild: BumbleBee From our initial analysis, BumbleBee is a custom new loader that is used by different IAB groups. This malware was observed injecting Cobalt Strike shellcodes in memory and using several tactics, techniques, and procedures (TTPs) in order to compromise the victim’s environment. As part of the campaign, the threat actors abuse spoofed companies' identities (like fake employee email addresses, fake websites, etc.) and use legitimate public storage services to deliver the malicious ISO image file. The ISO image file is responsible for luring the victim to execute the BumbleBee malware. We've seen Living Off the Land Binaries ( LOLBins ) execution with rundll32 , which allows threat actors to avoid defenses. BumbleBee also creates a scheduled task on the compromised host for persistence and executes a Visual Basic script via the scheduled task. The IAB relies on the user (victim) execution to execute the BumbleBee payload by luring the victim to mount an ISO image file and click on a Windows shortcut (LNK) file. The malware name, BumbleBee, was chosen because of its unique user agent, \"bumblebee,\" that was used as part of the communication with the command and control server (C2). Threat Analysis Group (TAG) shared observations on the financially motivated threat actor, EXOTIC LILY , that use the BumbleBee malware. In addition, TAG mentioned an interesting point of collaboration between EXOTIC LILY and the WIZARD SPIDER threat group. Orion’s observations This type of attack is new, and the cybersecurity community is still gathering data to glean more insights on the nature of this attack and its targets. Orion found a high number of targeted companies based in the US with the following distribution method that delivers the BumbleBee malware: Spear phishing email &gt; URL Link (TransferXL, TransferNow, WeTransfer) &gt; Zipped ISO &gt; ISO (contains the LNK file and the BumbleBee payload). You can see the execution flow in the image below. The infection flow We’ve handled several incident response (IR) cases where threat actors distributed BumbleBee malware. After the initial infection, the threat actors inject Cobalt Strike shellcode in memory and execute discovery commands to collect info about the victim’s network. We believe that threat actors performed this data collection in order to execute the next stage of the infection. The next stage is probably related to ransomware operations. We're still investigating IR cases in order to find conclusive evidence that the next stage delivers ransomware. On April 12, 2022, the BumbleBee IAB group was spotted using IMG file format in addition to ISO file format. You can see an example in the image below. The IMG file, which contains LNK and DLL Orion’s technical analysis Initial Access The BumbleBee payload was delivered via a spear phishing email that was sent from a spoofed email address. The email contains a URL link to the legitimate public storage service, TransferXL. Spear phishing email with a link to TransferXL Below you’ll see the legitimate public storage site, which leads the victim to the link to the malicious file. TransferXL legitimate public storage services Once they click download, the victim receives a ZIP folder that contains the malicious ISO image files. Spoofed company email address Execution Below is an example of what the ZIP file from the TransferXL link looks like. ZIP file download from TransferXL The ZIP file contains an ISO image file with the following name “ documents-04-106.iso.” Note that the following ISO image file name pattern was used for all the files that we have analyzed: documents-[0-9]{1,4}-[0-9]{1,4}\\.iso ISO image file From this step, threat actors rely on the victim (user) interaction with the ISO image file. The threat actors use a masquerading technique by setting the LNK file icon to be a folder icon in order to lure the victim to click on the LNK file: ISO image file contains LNK and DLL In addition, the DLL payload attribute is set as “Hidden” in order to hide the DLL payload from the user when interacting with the ISO image file: Hidden attribute for the DLL The masqueraded LNK file properties show that the execution target is as follows: C:\\Windows\\System32\\rundll32.exe settings.dll,IternalJob LNK executes the DLL via rundll32 command After the initial execution, the BumbleBee DLL is copied to the %programdata%/{RandomDir} directory. In addition to the DLL, a VBS script is also dropped to the same directory: [a-z]:\\\\programdata\\\\[a-z0-9]{16}\\\\[a-z0-9]{16}\\.[vbs|dll] TTPs indicators during the execution We have other artifacts from different IR cases, where we have observed the following activity. The screenshot below shows an event that detected a creation of a payload in the %ProgramData%\\{Random} directory the DLL payload is a copy of the initial BumbleBee loader that executed by Rundll32 from the ISO image file: Copy of the BumbleBee DLL to %Programdata% directory In other IR cases, we observed an execution flow that’s bit different. For example, a LNK that points to the following execution targets: cmd.exe /c start rundll32 neqw.dll,IternalJob rundll32.exe advpack.dll,RegisterOCX sysctl.exe Persistence We detected a scheduled task execution during the BumbleBee infection: Grandparent process: svchost.exe -k netsvcs -p -s Schedule Parent process: wscript.exe [a-z]:\\\\programdata\\\\[a-z0-9]{16}\\\\[a-z0-9]{16}\\.vbs Child process: rundll32.exe [a-z]:\\\\programdata\\\\[a-z0-9]{16}\\\\[a-z0-9]{16}\\.dll,{Export} Strings from the BumbleBee loader show the VBS script and the execution method We also observed WMI execution. The VBS file that was executed via a scheduled task, was also executed through WMI: Grandparent process: svchost.exe -k DcomLaunch Parent process: wmiprvse.exe -Embedding Child process: wscript.exe [a-z]:\\\\programdata\\\\[a-z0-9]{16}\\\\[a-z0-9]{16}\\.vbs Strings from the Bumblebee loader show the WMI Win32_Process execution Defense Evasion In our labs, we observed that BumbleBee uses several anti-VM methods to avoid detection. One of the anti-VM checks is related to the VirtualBox product: Check for lpWindowName if matches VirtualBox Other anti-VM artifacts were found after unpacking, as can be seen in the following strings: List of strings that are related to VMware and VirtualBox BumbleBee also detects if it is running within a VM by checking for known services that are related to different VM products: List of services that are related to VM products BumbleBee checks whether certain user names reside in the victim’s machine by comparing against a hardcoded list of user names. This allows BumbleBee to detect sandboxes and labs that are used for malware analysis: List of hardcoded usernames which are related to sandboxes and labs In addition, it uses WMI queries to collect system details and information: SELECT * FROM Win32_BaseBoard SELECT * FROM Win32_Bus SELECT * FROM Win32_ComputerSystem SELECT * FROM Win32_Fan SELECT * FROM Win32_NTEventlogFile SELECT * FROM Win32_OperatingSystem SELECT * FROM Win32_PnPDevice SELECT * FROM Win32_PnPEntity Discovery We found that the threat actors used the AdFind tool to enumerate and map the victim’s network. The ADFind tool was found in the %ProgramData% directory. In the instance we observed, the following commands were used: adfind.exe -gcb -sc trustdmp adfind.exe -f \"(objectcategory=group)\" adfind.exe -f \"(objectcategory=organizationalUnit)\" adfind.exe -f \"objectcategory=computer\" adfind.exe -f \"(objectcategory=person)\" Command and Control After the initial execution, the BumbleBee process (Rundll32) communicated with the Command-and-Control server (C2). We’ve seen several C2 servers from different IR cases: IP: 23.82.19[.]208:443 IP: 192.236.198[.]63:433 IP: 45.147.229[.]177:433 Example of the unique User-Agent: BumbleBee in the payload’s memory Additional reference to the BumbleBee malware name All the collected system and network information is sent to the C2 server, which sends back a response containing the next step/command to execute based on that info. BumbleBee binary analysis In this section, we will cover some interesting indicators and artifacts that highlighted the BumbleBee actions and heuristics. These artifacts also help us to identify the BumbleBee malware. We analyzed several payloads and all of them had the same artifacts. After unpacking the BumbleBee loader and by searching in the metadata of the unpacked payload, we identified BumbleBee’s internal name, “LdrAddx64.dll,” and two export functions – “IternalJob” and “SetPath.” BumbleBee internal name, export functions, and TimeDateStamp In the image below, we found the BumbleBee internal name and export function inside the process Rundll32.exe that executed the BumbleBee DLL loader: Bumblebee’s internal name and the export functions names in the memory By inspecting the unpacked BumbleBee sections, we discovered that the .data section contains two executables: PEStudio shows the unpacked Bumblebee section and highlighted the .data section We extracted the two hidden payloads from the .data section by using Hex-Editor tool: Hex-Editor shows 3 MZ headers: the first one is the Bumblebee, and the other two are additional payloads The first payload from the .data section is a 32-bit DLL payload: PEStudio showing the payload’s metadata We found a few interesting functions in the payload strings indicating that this payload has process injection capabilities. For example, “CreateProcess,” “NtWriteVirtualMemory,” “CreateRemoteThread,”and “WinExec.” PEStudio showing the payload’s strings that could be related to process injection The second payload that we extracted from the .data section is a 64-bit DLL payload: PEStudio showing the payload’s metadata We analyzed the payload binary and noticed that this payload is responsible for communicating with BumbleBee’s C2 server: In the strings we can see the C2 server’s IP address and port Both DLL payloads have the same internal name “RapportGP.dll.” An interesting point regarding the payloads internal name is that there is a legitimate DLL named “RapportGP.dll” that is part of a “Trusteer Ltd” product from a computer security division of IBM. Payloads internal name and TimeDateStamp Final notes BumbleBee threat actors are not the first to change the initial access method from malicious office documents to malicious ISO image files. The ISO image file abuse was also seen a few years ago, but in recent months, we have observed an increase in “ISO campaigns.” Different threat actors abuse ISO image files to deliver their payloads. For example, BazarISO deploys Bazarloader, and IcedID started to use ISO image files instead of MalDocs like in the two examples below. Documents-17.iso (Bazarloader) Invoice_pdf_1.iso (IcedID) In most of the cases, we’ve seen that during different IR cases, the campaigns escalated to full-blown ransomware attacks. We believe that IAB groups work and collaborate with ransomware affiliates like CONTI, LockBit, AvosLocker, and more. For example, we observed an IcedID infection that leads to CONTI ransomware attack (Shelob Moonlight). The Orion team is constantly monitoring BumbleBee and the IAB group's activities closely and analyzing them to better understand their motivation. As we learn more, we will publish our findings and artifacts to share additional insights for BumbleBee infection to ransomware post-attack chain. We're expecting to see more malware campaigns that will use the ISO delivery method in the near future. So, stay vigilant. As a final note, we’d like to share these indicators of compromise with you. Indicators of compromise: We hope this was helpful. And remember to check our blog page and follow us on social media to see when we publish updates. Have questions? Let us know     <script id="page-critical-js" class="ignore-script">
        // window.fbq = function() {};
        // window.rdt = function() {};
        document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', () => {
            setTimeout(initGTM, 3500);
        });
        document.addEventListener('scroll', initGTMOnEvent);
        document.addEventListener('mousemove', initGTMOnEvent);
        document.addEventListener('touchstart', initGTMOnEvent);

        function initGTMOnEvent (event) {
            initGTM();
            event.currentTarget.removeEventListener(event.type, initGTMOnEvent);
        }

        function initGTM () {
            if (window.gtmDidInit) {
                return false;
            }
            window.gtmDidInit = true;

            (function(w,d,s,l,i){w[l]=w[l]||[];w[l].push({'gtm.start':new Date().getTime(),event:'gtm.js'});var f=d.getElementsByTagName(s)[0], j=d.createElement(s),dl=l!='dataLayer'?'&l='+l:'';j.async=true;j.src= 'https://www.googletagmanager.com/gtm.js?id='+i+dl;f.parentNode.insertBefore(j,f);})(window,document,'script','dataLayer','GTM-T9F8RFV')
        }

        document.addEventListener('scroll', loadMegaMenuImagesOnEvent);
        document.addEventListener('mousemove', loadMegaMenuImagesOnEvent);
        document.addEventListener('touchstart', loadMegaMenuImagesOnEvent);

        function loadMegaMenuImagesOnEvent(event) {
            loadMegaMenuImages();
            event.currentTarget.removeEventListener(event.type, loadMegaMenuImagesOnEvent);
        }

        function loadMegaMenuImages() {
            const images = document.querySelectorAll('.col-nav img[data-src]');
            images.forEach((img) => {
                img.src = img.getAttribute('data-src');
                img.removeAttribute('data-src');
            });
        }

        function storeUTMParams() {
            const params = new URLSearchParams(window.location.search);

            // Store all UTM parameters
            params.forEach((value, key) => {
                if (key.includes('utm_')) {
                    localStorage.setItem(key, value);
                }
            });
        }
        document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', storeUTMParams);

        function getStoredUTMParams() {
            const storedUTMParams = {};

            for (let i = 0; i < localStorage.length; i++) {
                const key = localStorage.key(i);
                if (key.includes('utm_')) {
                    storedUTMParams[key] = localStorage.getItem(key);
                }
            }

            return storedUTMParams;
        }

        function addUTMFieldsToLinks() {
            const storedUTMParams = getStoredUTMParams();
            const links = document.querySelectorAll('a');

            links.forEach((link) => {
                if (!link.href.includes(window.location.origin)) {
                    return;
                }
                const url = new URL(link.href);

                for (const [key, value] of Object.entries(storedUTMParams)) {
                    url.searchParams.set(key, value);
                }

                link.href = url.toString();
            });
        }

        function setUTMParams() {
            const storedUTMParams = getStoredUTMParams();

            // update all fields with stored utm params
            for (const [key, value] of Object.entries(storedUTMParams)) {
                const fields = document.querySelectorAll(`input[name="${key}"], input[name="${key.toUpperCase()}"], input[name="${key.toLowerCase()}"]`);
                fields.forEach((field) => {
                    field.value = value;
                });
            }
        }

        // add utm params to all internal links
        document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', () => {
            addUTMFieldsToLinks()
            setUTMParams();
        });

        document.addEventListener('popupLoaded', () => {
            setUTMParams();
        });


        // Prevent console errors
 
        // Suppress uncaught errors
        window.onerror = function () {
            // Suppress uncaught JavaScript errors
            return true; // Prevent error from being logged in the console
        };
 

        const originalError = console.error;

        console.error = function (...args) {
            // Suppress only specific errors
            // if (args[0]?.includes('specific error text')) {
            //     return;
            // }
            // originalError.apply(console, args); // Log other errors
            return;
        };
    </script>

</style><script>
(function () {
  const categoryImageMap = {
    "Ransomware": "/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/CN_blog-thumb_M.jpg",
    "Actionable Insights": "/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/CN_blog-thumb_J.jpg",
    "XDR": "/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/CN_blog-thumb_C.jpg",
    "Research Reports & Alerts": "/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/CN_blog-thumb_P.jpg",
    "Threat Alerts": "/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/CN_blog-thumb_D.jpg",
    "Incident Response": "/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/CN_blog-thumb_E.jpg",
    "Lighthouse": "/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/CN_blog-thumb_E.jpg"
  };

  function overrideAllImages(context) {
  context.querySelectorAll(".cs-res-grid").forEach(function (grid) {
    grid.querySelectorAll(".ue_post_grid_item").forEach(function (postEl) {
      const categoryLinks = postEl.querySelectorAll(".ue-grid-item-category a");
      const imageEl = postEl.querySelector(".uc_post_image img");

      if (imageEl && categoryLinks.length > 0) {
        // Collect all category names
        const categories = Array.from(categoryLinks).map(link => link.textContent.trim());

        // Find the first category that has a mapped image
        const matchedCategory = categories.find(cat => categoryImageMap.hasOwnProperty(cat));

        if (matchedCategory) {
          const replacement = categoryImageMap[matchedCategory];
          imageEl.src = replacement;
          imageEl.alt = `Image for ${matchedCategory}`;
        }
      }
    });
  });
}

  document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function () {
    const runOverrides = () => overrideAllImages(document);

    // Initial run after Elementor finishes rendering
    setTimeout(runOverrides, 800);

    // Observe for pagination / dynamic content
    const observer = new MutationObserver(() => runOverrides());
    observer.observe(document.body, {
      childList: true,
      subtree: true
    });

    // Fallback: rerun every 2 seconds
    setInterval(runOverrides, 2000);
  });
})();
</script>				</div>

<script>
(function () {
  const categoryImageMap = {
    "Ransomware": "/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/CN_blog-thumb_M.jpg",
    "Actionable Insights": "/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/CN_blog-thumb_J.jpg",
    "XDR": "/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/CN_blog-thumb_C.jpg",
    "Research Reports & Alerts": "/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/CN_blog-thumb_P.jpg",
    "Threat Alerts": "/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/CN_blog-thumb_D.jpg",
    "Incident Response": "/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/CN_blog-thumb_E.jpg",
    "Lighthouse": "/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/CN_blog-thumb_E.jpg"
  };

  function overrideAllImages(context) {
  context.querySelectorAll(".cs-res-grid").forEach(function (grid) {
    grid.querySelectorAll(".ue_post_grid_item").forEach(function (postEl) {
      const categoryLinks = postEl.querySelectorAll(".ue-grid-item-category a");
      const imageEl = postEl.querySelector(".uc_post_image img");

      if (imageEl && categoryLinks.length > 0) {
        // Collect all category names
        const categories = Array.from(categoryLinks).map(link => link.textContent.trim());

        // Find the first category that has a mapped image
        const matchedCategory = categories.find(cat => categoryImageMap.hasOwnProperty(cat));

        if (matchedCategory) {
          const replacement = categoryImageMap[matchedCategory];
          imageEl.src = replacement;
          imageEl.alt = `Image for ${matchedCategory}`;
        }
      }
    });
  });
}

  document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function () {
    const runOverrides = () => overrideAllImages(document);

    // Initial run after Elementor finishes rendering
    setTimeout(runOverrides, 800);

    // Observe for pagination / dynamic content
    const observer = new MutationObserver(() => runOverrides());
    observer.observe(document.body, {
      childList: true,
      subtree: true
    });

    // Fallback: rerun every 2 seconds
    setInterval(runOverrides, 2000);
  });
})();
</script>
				</div>
				</div>
				</div>

		<div class="elementor-element elementor-element-e2e2abf e-con-full e-grid animated-slow elementor-invisible e-con e-child" data-id="e2e2abf" data-element_type="container" data-settings="{&quot;animation&quot;:&quot;fadeInRight&quot;,&quot;animation_delay&quot;:100,&quot;background_background&quot;:&quot;classic&quot;}">
		<div class="elementor-element elementor-element-ac432c1 e-con-full e-flex e-con e-child" data-id="ac432c1" data-element_type="container">
				<div class="elementor-element elementor-element-6aa4004 elementor-widget elementor-widget-image" data-id="6aa4004" data-element_type="widget" data-widget_type="image.default">
				<div class="elementor-widget-container">

				<div class="elementor-element elementor-element-099b252 cn-post-info elementor-widget elementor-widget-article_info_widget" data-id="099b252" data-element_type="widget" data-widget_type="article_info_widget.default">
				<div class="elementor-widget-container">
					<span class="post-date">April 14, 2022</span><span class="post-author">by: Max Malyutin – Orion Threat Research Team Leader</span>				</div>
				</div>
				<div class="elementor-element elementor-element-6f5ac28c elementor-invisible elementor-widget elementor-widget-theme-post-content" data-id="6f5ac28c" data-element_type="widget" data-settings="{&quot;_animation&quot;:&quot;fadeIn&quot;}" data-widget_type="theme-post-content.default">
				<div class="elementor-widget-container">
					<p><span class="ui-provider a b c d e f g h i j k l m n o p q r s t u v w x y z ab ac ae af ag ah ai aj ak" dir="ltr">Cynet’s Threat Research and Intelligence team recently discovered a new malware campaign called BumbleBee. The campaign is unique in its use of Initial Access Brokers’ (IAB) tactics to gain access to victims’ machines. In this post, we will cover what this campaign is, and how the IAB distributes the BumbleBee malware and its TTPs. We will also explain each TTP according to the MITRE ATT&amp;CK model, and its purpose.</span></p>
<h1>A new campaign in the wild: BumbleBee</h1>
<p>From our initial analysis, BumbleBee is a custom new loader that is used by different IAB groups. This malware was observed injecting <a href="https://attack.mitre.org/software/S0154/">Cobalt Strike</a> shellcodes in memory and using several tactics, techniques, and procedures (TTPs) in order to compromise the victim’s environment.</p>
<p>As part of the campaign, the threat actors abuse spoofed companies&#8217; identities (like fake employee email addresses, fake websites, etc.) and use legitimate public storage services to deliver the malicious ISO image file. The ISO image file is responsible for luring the victim to execute the BumbleBee malware.</p>
<p>We&#8217;ve seen Living Off the Land Binaries (<a href="https://lolbas-project.github.io/">LOLBins</a>) execution with <a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/011/">rundll32</a>, which allows threat actors to avoid defenses. BumbleBee also creates a <a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/005/">scheduled task</a> on the compromised host for persistence and executes a <a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1059/005/">Visual Basic script</a> via the scheduled task. The IAB relies on the <a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1204/002/">user (victim) execution to execute</a> the BumbleBee payload by luring the victim to mount an ISO image file and click on a Windows shortcut (LNK) file.</p>
<p>The malware name, BumbleBee, was chosen because of its unique user agent, &#8220;bumblebee,&#8221; that was used as part of the communication with the command and control server (C2).</p>
<p>Threat Analysis Group (TAG) shared observations on the financially motivated threat actor, <a href="https://blog.google/threat-analysis-group/exposing-initial-access-broker-ties-conti/">EXOTIC LILY</a>, that use the BumbleBee malware. In addition, TAG mentioned an interesting point of collaboration between EXOTIC LILY and the <a href="https://attack.mitre.org/groups/G0102/">WIZARD SPIDER</a> threat group.</p>
<h1>Orion’s observations</h1>
<p>This type of attack is new, and the cybersecurity community is still gathering data to glean more insights on the nature of this attack and its targets.</p>
<p>Orion found a high number of targeted companies based in the US with the following distribution method that delivers the BumbleBee malware: Spear phishing email &gt; URL Link (TransferXL, TransferNow, WeTransfer) &gt; Zipped ISO &gt; ISO (contains the LNK file and the BumbleBee payload).</p>
<p>You can see the execution flow in the image below.</p>
<p><img decoding="async" width="1462" height="537" class="wp-image-42735 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%201462%20537'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Diagram Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/diagram-description-automatically-generated-6.png 1462w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/diagram-description-automatically-generated-6-300x110.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/diagram-description-automatically-generated-6-1024x376.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/diagram-description-automatically-generated-6-768x282.png 768w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 1462px) 100vw, 1462px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/diagram-description-automatically-generated-6.png" /><noscript><img decoding="async" width="1462" height="537" class="wp-image-42735 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/diagram-description-automatically-generated-6.png" alt="Diagram Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/diagram-description-automatically-generated-6.png 1462w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/diagram-description-automatically-generated-6-300x110.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/diagram-description-automatically-generated-6-1024x376.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/diagram-description-automatically-generated-6-768x282.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1462px) 100vw, 1462px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>The infection flow</em></p>
<p>We’ve handled several incident response (IR) cases where threat actors distributed BumbleBee malware. After the initial infection, the threat actors inject Cobalt Strike shellcode in memory and execute discovery commands to collect info about the victim’s network. We believe that threat actors performed this data collection in order to execute the next stage of the infection.</p>
<p>The next stage is probably related to ransomware operations. We&#8217;re still investigating IR cases in order to find conclusive evidence that the next stage delivers ransomware.</p>
<p>On April 12, 2022, the BumbleBee IAB group was spotted using IMG file format in addition to ISO file format.</p>
<p>You can see an example in the image below.</p>
<p><img decoding="async" width="993" height="327" class="wp-image-42737 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20993%20327'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Graphical user interface, application Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-22.png 993w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-22-300x99.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-22-768x253.png 768w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 993px) 100vw, 993px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-22.png" /><noscript><img decoding="async" width="993" height="327" class="wp-image-42737 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-22.png" alt="Graphical user interface, application Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-22.png 993w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-22-300x99.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-22-768x253.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 993px) 100vw, 993px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>The IMG file, which contains LNK and DLL</em></p>
<h1>Orion’s technical analysis</h1>
<h3><strong><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/tactics/TA0001/">Initial Access</a></strong></h3>
<p>The BumbleBee payload was delivered via a spear phishing email that was sent from a spoofed email address. The email contains a URL link to the legitimate public storage service, TransferXL.</p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><img decoding="async" width="1618" height="509" class="wp-image-42738 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%201618%20509'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Graphical user interface, application Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-23.png 1618w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-23-300x94.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-23-1024x322.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-23-768x242.png 768w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-23-1536x483.png 1536w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 1618px) 100vw, 1618px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-23.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1618" height="509" class="wp-image-42738 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-23.png" alt="Graphical user interface, application Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-23.png 1618w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-23-300x94.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-23-1024x322.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-23-768x242.png 768w, with a link to TransferXL</em></p>
<p>Below you’ll see the legitimate public storage site, which leads the victim to the link to the malicious file.</p>
<p><img decoding="async" width="1430" height="657" class="wp-image-42741 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%201430%20657'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="A picture containing text Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-text-description-automatical-7.png 1430w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-text-description-automatical-7-300x138.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-text-description-automatical-7-1024x470.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-text-description-automatical-7-768x353.png 768w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 1430px) 100vw, 1430px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-text-description-automatical-7.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1430" height="657" class="wp-image-42741 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-text-description-automatical-7.png" alt="A picture containing text Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-text-description-automatical-7.png 1430w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-text-description-automatical-7-300x138.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-text-description-automatical-7-1024x470.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-text-description-automatical-7-768x353.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1430px) 100vw, 1430px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>TransferXL legitimate public storage services</em></p>
<p>Once they click download, the victim receives a ZIP folder that contains the malicious ISO image files.</p>
<p><img decoding="async" width="395" height="323" class="wp-image-42748 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20395%20323'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Diagram, application Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/diagram-application-description-automatically-ge-1.png 395w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/diagram-application-description-automatically-ge-1-300x245.png 300w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 395px) 100vw, 395px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/diagram-application-description-automatically-ge-1.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="395" height="323" class="wp-image-42748 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/diagram-application-description-automatically-ge-1.png" alt="Diagram, application Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/diagram-application-description-automatically-ge-1.png 395w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/diagram-application-description-automatically-ge-1-300x245.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 395px) 100vw, 395px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>Spoofed company email address </em></p>
<h3><strong><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/tactics/TA0002/">Execution</a></strong></h3>
<p>Below is an example of what the ZIP file from the TransferXL link looks like.</p>
<p><img decoding="async" width="668" height="121" class="wp-image-42750 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20668%20121'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Graphical user interface, text, application Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-32.png 668w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-32-300x54.png 300w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 668px) 100vw, 668px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-32.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="668" height="121" class="wp-image-42750 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-32.png" alt="Graphical user interface, text, application Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-32.png 668w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-32-300x54.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 668px) 100vw, 668px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>ZIP file download from TransferXL</em></p>
<p>The ZIP file contains an ISO image file with the following name “<em>documents-04-106.iso.” </em>Note that the following ISO image file name pattern was used for all the files that we have analyzed:</p>
<ul>
<li><em>documents-[0-9]{1,4}-[0-9]{1,4}\.iso</em></li>
</ul>
<p><img decoding="async" width="1284" height="449" class="wp-image-42751 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%201284%20449'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Graphical user interface, text, application Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-33.png 1284w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-33-300x105.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-33-1024x358.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-33-768x269.png 768w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 1284px) 100vw, 1284px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-33.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1284" height="449" class="wp-image-42751 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-33.png" alt="Graphical user interface, text, application Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-33.png 1284w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-33-300x105.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-33-1024x358.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-33-768x269.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1284px) 100vw, 1284px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>ISO image file</em></p>
<p>From this step, threat actors rely on the victim (user) interaction with the ISO image file. The threat actors use a masquerading technique by setting the LNK file icon to be a folder icon in order to lure the victim to click on the LNK file:</p>
<p><img decoding="async" width="1237" height="442" class="wp-image-42752 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%201237%20442'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Graphical user interface Description automatically generated with low confidence" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-description-automaticall-7.png 1237w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-description-automaticall-7-300x107.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-description-automaticall-7-1024x366.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-description-automaticall-7-768x274.png 768w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 1237px) 100vw, 1237px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-description-automaticall-7.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1237" height="442" class="wp-image-42752 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-description-automaticall-7.png" alt="Graphical user interface Description automatically generated with low confidence" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-description-automaticall-7.png 1237w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-description-automaticall-7-300x107.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-description-automaticall-7-1024x366.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-description-automaticall-7-768x274.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1237px) 100vw, 1237px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>ISO image file contains LNK and DLL</em></p>
<p>In addition, the DLL payload attribute is set as “Hidden” in order to hide the DLL payload from the user when interacting with the ISO image file:</p>
<p><img decoding="async" width="351" height="499" class="wp-image-42753 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20351%20499'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Graphical user interface, text, application, email Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-email-20.png 351w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-email-20-211x300.png 211w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 351px) 100vw, 351px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-email-20.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="351" height="499" class="wp-image-42753 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-email-20.png" alt="Graphical user interface, text, application, email Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-email-20.png 351w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-email-20-211x300.png 211w" sizes="(max-width: 351px) 100vw, 351px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>Hidden attribute for the DLL</em></p>
<p>The masqueraded LNK file properties show that the execution target is as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li><em>C:\Windows\System32\rundll32.exe settings.dll,IternalJob</em></li>
</ul>
<p><img decoding="async" width="351" height="499" class="wp-image-42754 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20351%20499'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Graphical user interface, text, application, email Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-email-21.png 351w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-email-21-211x300.png 211w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 351px) 100vw, 351px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-email-21.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="351" height="499" class="wp-image-42754 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-email-21.png" alt="Graphical user interface, text, application, email Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-email-21.png 351w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-email-21-211x300.png 211w" sizes="(max-width: 351px) 100vw, 351px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>LNK executes the DLL via rundll32 command</em></p>
<p>After the initial execution, the BumbleBee DLL is copied to the %programdata%/{RandomDir} directory. In addition to the DLL, a VBS script is also dropped to the same directory:</p>
<ul>
<li>[a-z]:\\programdata\\[a-z0-9]{16}\\[a-z0-9]{16}\.[vbs|dll]</li>
</ul>
<p><img decoding="async" width="1320" height="263" class="wp-image-42755 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%201320%20263'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Graphical user interface, text, application Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-34.png 1320w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-34-300x60.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-34-1024x204.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-34-768x153.png 768w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 1320px) 100vw, 1320px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-34.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1320" height="263" class="wp-image-42755 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-34.png" alt="Graphical user interface, text, application Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-34.png 1320w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-34-300x60.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-34-1024x204.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-34-768x153.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1320px) 100vw, 1320px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>TTPs indicators during the execution</em></p>
<p>We have other artifacts from different IR cases, where we have observed the following activity. The screenshot below shows an event that detected a creation of a payload in the %ProgramData%\{Random} directory the DLL payload is a copy of the initial BumbleBee loader that executed by Rundll32 from the ISO image file:</p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><img decoding="async" width="1797" height="157" class="wp-image-42756 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%201797%20157'%3E%3C/svg%3E" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/word-image-31.png 1797w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/word-image-31-300x26.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/word-image-31-1024x89.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/word-image-31-768x67.png 768w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/word-image-31-1536x134.png 1536w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 1797px) 100vw, 1797px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/word-image-31.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1797" height="157" class="wp-image-42756 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/word-image-31.png" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/word-image-31.png 1797w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/word-image-31-300x26.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/word-image-31-1024x89.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/word-image-31-768x67.png 768w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/word-image-31-1536x134.png 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 1797px) 100vw, 1797px" /></noscript><em>Copy of the BumbleBee DLL to %Programdata% directory</em></p>
<p>In other IR cases, we observed an execution flow that’s bit different. For example, a LNK that points to the following execution targets:</p>
<ul>
<li>cmd.exe /c start rundll32 neqw.dll,IternalJob</li>
<li>rundll32.exe advpack.dll,RegisterOCX sysctl.exe</li>
</ul>
<h3><strong><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/tactics/TA0003/">Persistence</a></strong></h3>
<p>We detected a scheduled task execution during the BumbleBee infection:</p>
<table class=" aligncenter">
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Grandparent process:</strong>svchost.exe -k netsvcs -p -s Schedule<strong>Parent process:</strong></p>
<p>wscript.exe [a-z]:\\programdata\\[a-z0-9]{16}\\[a-z0-9]{16}\.vbs</p>
<p><strong>Child process:</strong></p>
<p>rundll32.exe [a-z]:\\programdata\\[a-z0-9]{16}\\[a-z0-9]{16}\.dll,{Export}</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p style="text-align: center;"><img decoding="async" width="1537" height="266" class="wp-image-42757 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%201537%20266'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Graphical user interface, text, application Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-35.png 1537w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-35-300x52.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-35-1024x177.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-35-768x133.png 768w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 1537px) 100vw, 1537px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-35.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1537" height="266" class="wp-image-42757 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-35.png" alt="Graphical user interface, text, application Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-35.png 1537w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-35-300x52.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-35-1024x177.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-35-768x133.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1537px) 100vw, 1537px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>Strings from the BumbleBee loader show the VBS script and the execution method</em></p>
<p>We also observed WMI execution. The VBS file that was executed via a scheduled task, was also executed through WMI:</p>
<table class=" aligncenter">
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>Grandparent process:</strong>svchost.exe -k DcomLaunch<strong>Parent process:</strong></p>
<p>wmiprvse.exe -Embedding</p>

<p>wscript.exe [a-z]:\\programdata\\[a-z0-9]{16}\\[a-z0-9]{16}\.vbs</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<h3><strong><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/tactics/TA0005/">Defense Evasion</a></strong></h3>
<p>In our labs, we observed that BumbleBee uses several anti-VM methods to avoid detection.</p>
<p>One of the anti-VM checks is related to the VirtualBox product:</p>
<p><img decoding="async" width="350" height="334" class="wp-image-42759 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20350%20334'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Graphical user interface, text, application Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-36.png 350w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-36-300x286.png 300w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 350px) 100vw, 350px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-36.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="350" height="334" class="wp-image-42759 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-36.png" alt="Graphical user interface, text, application Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-36.png 350w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-36-300x286.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 350px) 100vw, 350px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>Check for lpWindowName if matches VirtualBox</em></p>
<p>Other anti-VM artifacts were found after unpacking, as can be seen in the following strings:</p>
<p><img decoding="async" width="489" height="757" class="wp-image-42760 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20489%20757'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Table Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-description-automatically-generated-7.png 489w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-description-automatically-generated-7-194x300.png 194w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 489px) 100vw, 489px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-description-automatically-generated-7.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="489" height="757" class="wp-image-42760 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-description-automatically-generated-7.png" alt="Table Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-description-automatically-generated-7.png 489w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-description-automatically-generated-7-194x300.png 194w" sizes="(max-width: 489px) 100vw, 489px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>List of strings that are related to VMware and VirtualBox</em></p>
<p>BumbleBee also detects if it is running within a VM by checking for known services that are related to different VM products:</p>
<p><img decoding="async" width="554" height="317" class="wp-image-42761 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20554%20317'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Table Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-description-automatically-generated-8.png 554w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-description-automatically-generated-8-300x172.png 300w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 554px) 100vw, 554px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-description-automatically-generated-8.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="554" height="317" class="wp-image-42761 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-description-automatically-generated-8.png" alt="Table Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-description-automatically-generated-8.png 554w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-description-automatically-generated-8-300x172.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 554px) 100vw, 554px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>List of services that are related to VM products </em></p>
<p>BumbleBee checks whether certain user names reside in the victim’s machine by comparing against a hardcoded list of user names. This allows BumbleBee to detect sandboxes and labs that are used for malware analysis:</p>
<p><img decoding="async" width="670" height="324" class="wp-image-42762 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20670%20324'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Table Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-description-automatically-generated-9.png 670w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-description-automatically-generated-9-300x145.png 300w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 670px) 100vw, 670px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-description-automatically-generated-9.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="670" height="324" class="wp-image-42762 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-description-automatically-generated-9.png" alt="Table Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-description-automatically-generated-9.png 670w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-description-automatically-generated-9-300x145.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 670px) 100vw, 670px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>List of hardcoded usernames which are related to sandboxes and labs </em></p>
<p>In addition, it uses WMI queries to collect system details and information:</p>
<ul>
<li>SELECT * FROM Win32_BaseBoard</li>
<li>SELECT * FROM Win32_Bus</li>
<li>SELECT * FROM Win32_ComputerSystem</li>
<li>SELECT * FROM Win32_Fan</li>
<li>SELECT * FROM Win32_NTEventlogFile</li>
<li>SELECT * FROM Win32_OperatingSystem</li>
<li>SELECT * FROM Win32_PnPDevice</li>
<li>SELECT * FROM Win32_PnPEntity</li>
</ul>
<h3><strong><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/tactics/TA0007/">Discovery</a></strong></h3>
<p>We found that the threat actors used the AdFind tool to enumerate and map the victim’s network. The ADFind tool was found in the %ProgramData% directory.</p>
<p>In the instance we observed, the following commands were used:</p>
<ul>
<li>adfind.exe -gcb -sc trustdmp</li>
<li>adfind.exe -f &#8220;(objectcategory=group)&#8221;</li>
<li>adfind.exe -f &#8220;(objectcategory=organizationalUnit)&#8221;</li>
<li>adfind.exe -f &#8220;objectcategory=computer&#8221;</li>
<li>adfind.exe -f &#8220;(objectcategory=person)&#8221;</li>
</ul>
<h3><strong><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/tactics/TA0011/">Command and Control</a></strong></h3>
<p>After the initial execution, the BumbleBee process (Rundll32) communicated with the Command-and-Control server (C2). We’ve seen several C2 servers from different IR cases:</p>
<ul>
<li><em>IP: 23.82.19[.]208:443</em></li>
<li><em>IP: 192.236.198[.]63:433</em></li>
<li><em>IP: 45.147.229[.]177:433</em></li>
</ul>
<p><img decoding="async" width="1046" height="613" class="wp-image-42763 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%201046%20613'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Calendar Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/calendar-description-automatically-generated-3.png 1046w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/calendar-description-automatically-generated-3-300x176.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/calendar-description-automatically-generated-3-1024x600.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/calendar-description-automatically-generated-3-768x450.png 768w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 1046px) 100vw, 1046px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/calendar-description-automatically-generated-3.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1046" height="613" class="wp-image-42763 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/calendar-description-automatically-generated-3.png" alt="Calendar Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/calendar-description-automatically-generated-3.png 1046w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/calendar-description-automatically-generated-3-300x176.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/calendar-description-automatically-generated-3-1024x600.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/calendar-description-automatically-generated-3-768x450.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1046px) 100vw, 1046px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>Example of the unique User-Agent: BumbleBee in the payload’s memory </em></p>
<p><img decoding="async" width="599" height="55" class="wp-image-42764 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20599%2055'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Graphical user interface, application, website Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-website-de-3.png 599w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-website-de-3-300x28.png 300w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 599px) 100vw, 599px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-website-de-3.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="599" height="55" class="wp-image-42764 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-website-de-3.png" alt="Graphical user interface, application, website Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-website-de-3.png 599w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-website-de-3-300x28.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 599px) 100vw, 599px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em> Additional reference to the BumbleBee malware name </em></p>
<p>All the collected system and network information is sent to the C2 server, which sends back a response containing the next step/command to execute based on that info.</p>
<h1>BumbleBee binary analysis</h1>
<p>In this section, we will cover some interesting indicators and artifacts that highlighted the BumbleBee actions and heuristics. These artifacts also help us to identify the BumbleBee malware.</p>
<p>We analyzed several payloads and all of them had the same artifacts.</p>
<p>After unpacking the BumbleBee loader and by searching in the metadata of the unpacked payload, we identified BumbleBee’s internal name, “LdrAddx64.dll,” and two export functions – “IternalJob” and “SetPath.”</p>
<p><img decoding="async" width="679" height="392" class="wp-image-42765 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20679%20392'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Graphical user interface, text Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-description-automa-11.png 679w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-description-automa-11-300x173.png 300w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 679px) 100vw, 679px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-description-automa-11.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="679" height="392" class="wp-image-42765 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-description-automa-11.png" alt="Graphical user interface, text Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-description-automa-11.png 679w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-description-automa-11-300x173.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 679px) 100vw, 679px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>BumbleBee internal name, export functions, and TimeDateStamp</em></p>
<p>In the image below, we found the BumbleBee internal name and export function inside the process Rundll32.exe that executed the BumbleBee DLL loader:</p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><img decoding="async" width="1109" height="578" class="wp-image-42766 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%201109%20578'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Table, calendar Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-calendar-description-automatically-generat-1.png 1109w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-calendar-description-automatically-generat-1-300x156.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-calendar-description-automatically-generat-1-1024x534.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-calendar-description-automatically-generat-1-768x400.png 768w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 1109px) 100vw, 1109px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-calendar-description-automatically-generat-1.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1109" height="578" class="wp-image-42766 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-calendar-description-automatically-generat-1.png" alt="Table, calendar Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-calendar-description-automatically-generat-1.png 1109w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-calendar-description-automatically-generat-1-300x156.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-calendar-description-automatically-generat-1-1024x534.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/table-calendar-description-automatically-generat-1-768x400.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1109px) 100vw, 1109px" /></noscript><em>Bumblebee’s internal name and the export functions names in the memory</em></p>
<p>By inspecting the unpacked BumbleBee sections, we discovered that the .data section contains two executables:</p>
<p><img decoding="async" width="1497" height="426" class="wp-image-42767 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%201497%20426'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Graphical user interface, application Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-25.png 1497w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-25-300x85.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-25-1024x291.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-25-768x219.png 768w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 1497px) 100vw, 1497px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-25.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1497" height="426" class="wp-image-42767 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-25.png" alt="Graphical user interface, application Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-25.png 1497w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-25-300x85.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-25-1024x291.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-description-25-768x219.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1497px) 100vw, 1497px" /></noscript></p>

<p>We extracted the two hidden payloads from the .data section by using Hex-Editor tool:</p>
<p><img decoding="async" width="1284" height="735" class="wp-image-42768 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%201284%20735'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="A picture containing table Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-table-description-automatica-5.png 1284w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-table-description-automatica-5-300x172.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-table-description-automatica-5-1024x586.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-table-description-automatica-5-768x440.png 768w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 1284px) 100vw, 1284px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-table-description-automatica-5.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1284" height="735" class="wp-image-42768 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-table-description-automatica-5.png" alt="A picture containing table Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-table-description-automatica-5.png 1284w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-table-description-automatica-5-300x172.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-table-description-automatica-5-1024x586.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-table-description-automatica-5-768x440.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1284px) 100vw, 1284px" /></noscript></p>

<p>The first payload from the .data section is a 32-bit DLL payload:</p>
<p><img decoding="async" width="712" height="537" class="wp-image-42769 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20712%20537'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Graphical user interface, text, application Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-37.png 712w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-37-300x226.png 300w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 712px) 100vw, 712px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-37.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="712" height="537" class="wp-image-42769 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-37.png" alt="Graphical user interface, text, application Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-37.png 712w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-text-application-descr-37-300x226.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 712px) 100vw, 712px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>PEStudio showing the payload’s metadata </em></p>
<p>We found a few interesting functions in the payload strings indicating that this payload has process injection capabilities. For example, “CreateProcess,” “NtWriteVirtualMemory,” “CreateRemoteThread,”and “WinExec.”</p>
<p><img decoding="async" width="1051" height="670" class="wp-image-42770 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%201051%20670'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Graphical user interface, application, table Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-table-desc-2.png 1051w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-table-desc-2-300x191.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-table-desc-2-1024x653.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-table-desc-2-768x490.png 768w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 1051px) 100vw, 1051px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-table-desc-2.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1051" height="670" class="wp-image-42770 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-table-desc-2.png" alt="Graphical user interface, application, table Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-table-desc-2.png 1051w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-table-desc-2-300x191.png 300w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-table-desc-2-1024x653.png 1024w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-table-desc-2-768x490.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1051px) 100vw, 1051px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>PEStudio showing the payload’s strings that could be related to process injection </em></p>
<p>The second payload that we extracted from the .data section is a 64-bit DLL payload:</p>
<p><img decoding="async" width="716" height="538" class="wp-image-42771 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20716%20538'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="A picture containing graphical user interface Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-graphical-user-interface-des-2.png 716w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-graphical-user-interface-des-2-300x225.png 300w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 716px) 100vw, 716px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-graphical-user-interface-des-2.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="716" height="538" class="wp-image-42771 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-graphical-user-interface-des-2.png" alt="A picture containing graphical user interface Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-graphical-user-interface-des-2.png 716w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/a-picture-containing-graphical-user-interface-des-2-300x225.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 716px) 100vw, 716px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em> PEStudio showing the payload’s metadata </em></p>
<p>We analyzed the payload binary and noticed that this payload is responsible for communicating with BumbleBee’s C2 server:</p>
<p><img decoding="async" width="737" height="270" class="wp-image-42772 aligncenter" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20737%20270'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Graphical user interface, application, table Description automatically generated" data-lazy-srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-table-desc-3.png 737w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-table-desc-3-300x110.png 300w" data-lazy-sizes="(max-width: 737px) 100vw, 737px" data-lazy-src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-table-desc-3.png" /><noscript><img loading="lazy" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="737" height="270" class="wp-image-42772 aligncenter" src="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-table-desc-3.png" alt="Graphical user interface, application, table Description automatically generated" srcset="https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-table-desc-3.png 737w, https://www.cynet.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/graphical-user-interface-application-table-desc-3-300x110.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 737px) 100vw, 737px" /></noscript></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em> In the strings we can see the C2 server’s IP address and port </em></p>
<p>Both DLL payloads have the same internal name “RapportGP.dll.” An interesting point regarding the payloads internal name is that there is a legitimate DLL named “RapportGP.dll” that is part of a “Trusteer Ltd” product from a computer security division of IBM.</p>
